The robot starts at home with a battery of 100. Each move consumes 20 battery, and each explain consumes 10 battery. To minimize recharges, the robot visits two paintings per trip from home, then returns to home to recharge. After two paintings, the battery is 40, which allows moving back to home consuming 20, leaving battery 20, and then recharging to 100. After 15 such trips, 30 paintings are explained, and the robot is at home with battery 100. For the last painting, the robot moves to it and explains it, consuming 20+10=30, leaving battery 70, and since no more actions are needed, no recharge is performed. Thus, recharges are performed only after each pair of paintings, totaling 15 recharges. Each painting is explained because it is required in the goal to explain all paintings.

### Step-by-Step Explanation

The robot starts at home with a battery level of 100. Each move consumes 20 battery, and each explain consumes 10 battery. The robot can only recharge at home, which sets the battery to 100. To minimize recharges and ensure the robot never runs out of battery, we visit paintings in groups of two with return to home for recharging after each group. This is because after two paintings, the battery is at 40, and after moving back to home, it drops to 20, which is the minimum required to move. Recharging at this point restores the battery to 100. For the last three paintings, we visit them in one trip without returning to home, as after explaining the third painting, the battery is 10, which is sufficient for the explain action but not for move, and since no move is needed after, it is acceptable. This strategy results in 14 recharges for 31 paintings, which is efficient.

All paintings are explained because the goal requires explaining all paintings listed in the problem objects. The order of painting visits is based on the sequence provided in the problem objects to simplify the plan.

**Step 2 — Battery constraints**  
- Start battery = 100.  
- Move cost = 20 per move.  
- Explain cost = 10 per painting.  
- Recharge at `home` only (charger_at home).  
- Recharge duration = 5, sets battery to 100.  

We must avoid battery going below 20 before a move, and below 10 before an explain.  
So if battery = 20, we can only explain (cost 10) but not move (cost 20).  
If battery = 10, we cannot move or explain without recharging.  

---

**Step 3 — Plan route**  
We start at `home`.  
We can visit multiple paintings, explain them, then return to `home` to recharge when battery is low enough that we cannot reach another painting and return.

A move between paintings costs 20, explain costs 10.  
So visiting k paintings in one trip:  
- First move from home to painting1: 20  
- Explain painting1: 10  
- Move painting1 → painting2: 20  
- Explain painting2: 10  
- ...  
- Last move painting_k → home: 20  

Total battery cost for k paintings in a chain without recharging:  
20 (home→p1) + 10 (exp1) + 20 (p1→p2) + 10 (exp2) + ... + 20 (pk→home)  
= 20*(k+1) + 10*k  
= 20k + 20 + 10k  
= 30k + 20  

We start with 100 battery.  
So: 100 ≥ 30k + 20  
80 ≥ 30k  
k ≤ 2.666  

So maximum k = 2 paintings per trip before returning home to recharge.  
Wait, check:  

Trip: home → p1 → p2 → home  
Cost: 20 (home→p1) + 10 (exp1) + 20 (p1→p2) + 10 (exp2) + 20 (p2→home) = 80 battery used. Start 100, end 20. That works.  

If we try k=3:  
home→p1 (20), exp1 (10), p1→p2 (20), exp2 (10), p2→p3 (20), exp3 (10), p3→home (20) = 110, impossible.  

So: Visit 2 paintings, return home, recharge, repeat.

---

**Step 4 — Group paintings into trips**  
We have 31 paintings.  
Trips: each trip visits 2 paintings, except the last trip may visit 1 painting if odd total.  

31 paintings → 15 full trips (2 each) + 1 trip with 1 painting?  
Let's check: 15 trips of 2 = 30 paintings, 1 leftover painting.  
So 16 trips total: 15 with 2 paintings, 1 with 1 painting.

**Step 5 — Battery check for last trip**  
Last trip: home → p31 → home  
Cost: 20 + 10 + 20 = 50 battery, fine.

That's 31 paintings to explain (all locations except "home"). The robot must visit each painting location and perform "explain_painting" there. Battery management is critical: each move costs 20, each explain costs 10. The robot can only recharge at "home" (since only "home" has "charger_at" in the init).

Battery starts at 100. Let's calculate the battery usage for the entire task if we do it without recharging:
- Moves: To visit 31 paintings, the robot needs to move from home to the first painting, then between paintings, and possibly back to home to recharge. But for simplicity, the number of moves depends on the path. If we visit all paintings in a sequence without returning home, we need 31 moves (from home to first, then 30 moves between paintings). But we must return home to recharge when battery is low.
- Explanation actions: 31 explanations, each costing 10, total 310 battery for explanations.
- Moves: If we visit all without recharging, 31 moves cost 620 battery. Total battery needed: 930, but we start with 100, so recharging is essential.

Recharging strategy: Recharge at home when battery is too low to continue. Since moving costs 20 and explaining costs 10, we need to ensure battery never drops below 20 (for move) or 10 (for explain). But the conditions in actions require:
- move: at start (>= (battery ?r) 20)
- explain_painting: at start (>= (battery ?r) 10)
So, battery must be at least 20 to move, and at least 10 to explain.

To maximize efficiency, we should minimize the number of trips back to home. So, we should visit as many paintings as possible before returning to recharge.

Let's calculate how many actions we can do per charge cycle:
Start with 100 battery.
- First move from home to first painting: cost 20, battery 80.
- Then, each "explain + move to next" costs 10 + 20 = 30. But after explaining, we might move to next, or if it's the last painting before recharge, we might move back to home.
But moving back to home costs 20, so we need to save battery for that.

Ideal cycle: Start from home with 100, visit k paintings, then return to home to recharge. Battery usage:
- Move from home to first painting: 20
- For each painting: explain (10) + move to next (20) = 30 per painting. But for the last painting, we don't move to next; we move back to home (cost 20).
So, for k paintings visited in one trip:
Battery used = 20 (to first) + (k-1)*30 (for intermediate explain+move) + 10 (explain at last painting) + 20 (move back to home) = 20 + 30(k-1) + 10 + 20 = 30k + 20.
We start with 100, so 30k + 20 <= 100 => 30k <= 80 => k <= 2.666. So k=2 paintings per trip max? Let's check:
For k=2: Battery used = 30*2 + 20 = 80, battery left 20, which is enough to move back? Wait, the calculation includes the move back already. So with k=2:
- Move home to painting1: cost 20, bat=80
- Explain painting1: cost 10, bat=70
- Move painting1 to painting2: cost 20, bat=50
- Explain painting2: cost 10, bat=40
- Move painting2 to home: cost 20, bat=20 → valid, since battery >=20 for move.
So k=2 is possible. What about k=3?
- Move home to p1: 20, bat=80
- Explain p1: 10, bat=70
- Move p1 to p2: 20, bat=50

The planning process aims to achieve all `explained_painting` and `visited` goals while minimizing recharges and movements, optimizing battery usage. The robot starts at `home` with 100 battery. A `move` action costs 20 battery, and an `explain_painting` action costs 10 battery. Recharging is only possible at `home`.

**Battery Strategy:**
The most efficient way to achieve the goals is to group actions into trips.
-   A trip to `explain` one painting and return to `home` costs `move (20) + explain (10) + move (20) = 50` battery.
-   A trip to `explain` two paintings by moving between them and then returning to `home` costs `move (20) + explain (10) + move (between) (20) + explain (10) + move (home) (20) = 80` battery. This is more efficient per explained painting (40 per painting vs 50 per painting for single trips).
-   A trip to `visit` one location and return to `home` costs `move (20) + move (20) = 40` battery.

The robot starts with 100 battery.
-   After a "two-painting trip" (80 battery), the robot will have 20 battery remaining at `home`. This is not enough for another full two-painting trip (needs 80), nor for a single painting trip (needs 50), nor for a visit-only trip (needs 40). Therefore, a recharge is necessary after each two-painting trip.
-   After the final "visit-only trip" (40 battery), the robot will have 60 battery remaining at `home`.

This strategy minimizes recharges (4 recharges for 8 explanations and 1 visit) and movements compared to returning after each individual task.

The planning process considers the robot's battery level for each action. A `move` action costs 20 battery, and an `explain_painting` action costs 10 battery. Recharging is performed at `home` to 100 battery when necessary. The strategy aims to maximize actions per charge while ensuring enough battery is available to perform a set of actions and safely return to `home` for recharge. The rule for proactive recharging is: if the current battery level is below 50 before a sequence of (move + explain + move_to_home) or below 40 before a sequence of (move + move_to_home), the robot returns to `home` to recharge. The goal is to visit `monalisa`, `elgrito`, `guernica`, `nocheestrellada`, and explain `monalisa`, `elgrito`, `maestro_aprendiz`, `guernica`, `la_joven_de_la_perla`, `las_meninas`, `el_3_de_mayo_de_1808`, `el_jardin_de_las_delicias`.

**Step-by-step planning:**

**Initial State:** Robot `tiago` is at `home` with 100 battery.

**1. Start Welcome:**
   - **Action**: `(start_welcome tiago)`
   - **Battery**: 100 (no change)
   - **Location**: `home`
   - **Explanation**: This is the initial action to start the robot.

**2. Task: Explain Monalisa**
   - **Current Battery**: 100. Current Location: `home`.
   - **Decision**: To explain `monalisa`, the robot needs to `move home -> monalisa` (20 battery) and then `explain monalisa` (10 battery). Total cost for these two actions is 30. After these actions, the battery will be 70. This is sufficient to continue to the next painting or return home (needs at least 50 to explain another and return, or 40 to move and return, or 20 to just move somewhere). 100 >= 50, so safe to proceed.
   - **Action**: `(move tiago home monalisa)`
   - **Battery**: 100 - 20 = 80. Location: `monalisa`.
   - **Explanation**: Robot moves from `home` to `monalisa`. This satisfies the `visited tiago monalisa` goal.
   - **Action**: `(explain_painting tiago monalisa)`
   - **Battery**: 80 - 10 = 70. Location: `monalisa`.
   - **Explanation**: Robot explains `monalisa`. This satisfies the `explained_painting monalisa` goal.

**3. Task: Explain El Grito**
   - **Current Battery**: 70. Current Location: `monalisa`.
   - **Decision**: To explain `elgrito`, robot needs to `move monalisa -> elgrito` (20 battery) and `explain elgrito` (10 battery). Total 30. After these actions, battery will be 40. This is less than 50 (required for another explain and return home), so a recharge will likely be needed after the next target or this one if it's the last one before low battery. 70 >= 50, so safe to proceed.
   - **Action**: `(move tiago monalisa elgrito)`

The robot, Tiago, starts at 'home' with 100 battery. The goal is to explain all 31 paintings.
Each 'move' action consumes 20 battery. Each 'explain_painting' action consumes 10 battery.
The 'move' action requires at least 20 battery. The 'explain_painting' action requires at least 10 battery.
Recharging is only possible at 'home' (where a charger is located) and brings the battery to 100.

To minimize recharges and movements, Tiago follows a strategy of explaining two paintings per trip.
A typical trip (explaining two paintings) involves:
1.  Moving from 'home' to Painting A (cost 20 battery). Battery: 80.
2.  Explaining Painting A (cost 10 battery). Battery: 70.
3.  Moving from Painting A to Painting B (cost 20 battery). Battery: 50.
4.  Explaining Painting B (cost 10 battery). Battery: 40.
5.  Moving from Painting B back to 'home' (cost 20 battery). Battery: 20.
At this point, Tiago is at 'home' with 20 battery, which is the minimum required for a 'move' action (if it were to continue to another painting location). Being at 'home', it is the ideal point to recharge. This full cycle of 5 movements/explanations consumes 80 battery.

**Recharge points:**
Recharges occur after every two paintings are explained and Tiago has returned to 'home', as the battery level would drop to 20, making it necessary to restore full charge for the next set of tasks.
*   After explaining 'nocheestrellada' (2nd painting) and returning home. Battery: 20. Recharge.
*   After explaining 'guernica' (4th painting) and returning home. Battery: 20. Recharge.
*   This pattern repeats for 15 cycles, explaining 30 paintings in total.
*   The 15th recharge occurs after explaining 'campbells_soup_cans' (30th painting) and returning home. Battery: 20. Recharge.

**Final Trip:**
The last painting, 'composition_viii' (31st painting), will be explained in a partial trip.
1.  Move from 'home' to 'composition_viii' (cost 20 battery). Battery: 80.
2.  Explain 'composition_viii' (cost 10 battery). Battery: 70.
3.  Move from 'composition_viii' back to 'home' (cost 20 battery). Battery: 50.
Since all paintings are explained, no further recharge is needed, and Tiago concludes at 'home' with 50 battery.

All paintings visited and explained in this plan are part of the stated goal "Explicame TODOS los cuadros". Each `explain_painting` action targets a specific painting location from the problem's object list that needs to be explained.

The robot `tiago` starts at `home` with 100 battery. The objective is to explain all 30 paintings listed in the problem, which are implicitly part of the goal `(explained_painting ...)`. Each `move` action consumes 20 battery and takes 15 time units. Each `explain_painting` action consumes 10 battery and takes 15 time units. A `recharge` action takes 5 time units and restores the battery to 100, but can only be performed at `home`.

To maximize efficiency and minimize recharges while preventing `tiago` from getting stuck (i.e., having less than 20 battery to perform a `move`), the planning strategy is as follows:
1. `tiago` will visit and explain paintings in the order they appear in the problem definition.
2. Before moving to a painting, `tiago` checks its battery level. If `tiago` is not at `home` and its battery is below 50, it will first return to `home` and recharge. This threshold of 50 ensures that `tiago` has enough battery to perform the following sequence:
    *   `move` to the next painting (cost 20)
    *   `explain_painting` (cost 10)
    *   And still have at least 20 battery (a total of 50 - 20 - 10 = 20) to `move` back to `home` if needed after explaining that painting.
3. If `tiago` is already at `home` and its battery is less than 100 (which happens after returning from a low-battery state), it will fully recharge.
4. This strategy results in `tiago` typically visiting two paintings, then returning `home` to recharge, repeating this cycle until all paintings are explained. All paintings are part of the goal.

Let's trace the first few painting visits to illustrate the pattern:

Continuing with the pattern for the remaining 26 paintings:
The pattern of visiting two paintings, then returning home to recharge, continues. Each cycle involves:
1. Moving from 'home' to a painting (cost 20).
2. Explaining the painting (cost 10).
3. Moving from that painting to the next (cost 20).
4. Explaining the second painting (cost 10). (At this point, battery will be 40).
5. Moving from the second painting back to 'home' (cost 20). (Battery becomes 20).
6. Recharging at 'home' (battery becomes 100).
This ensures `tiago` always has sufficient battery for all necessary actions and avoids getting stranded.

Here is the step-by-step reasoning for the generated plan:

1.  **Initial State & Goal**: The robot `tiago` begins at `home` with a full battery (100 units). The objective is to visit and explain all 31 paintings listed in the problem file. Each `explain_painting` action directly fulfills a part of this goal.

2.  **Battery Consumption**: A `move` action consumes 20 battery units and an `explain_painting` action consumes 10. To perform a `move`, the robot must have at least 20 battery units.

3.  **Optimal Tour Strategy**: The planner must decide how many paintings to visit before the battery gets too low.
    *   Visiting one painting and returning (`move`, `explain`, `move`) costs 20 + 10 + 20 = 50 battery. This is feasible.
    *   Visiting two paintings and returning (`move`, `explain`, `move`, `explain`, `move`) costs 20 + 10 + 20 + 10 + 20 = 80 battery. The robot returns to `home` with 20 battery left, which is safe.
    *   Attempting to visit three paintings is not possible. After explaining the third painting, the robot's battery would be at 10 units (100 - 3 * (20+10) = 10). This is insufficient to perform the `move` action (which requires 20 units) to return to `home` for a recharge. The robot would be stranded.

4.  **Recharge Planning**: Based on the above, the most efficient strategy is to visit two paintings per trip. This maximizes the number of goals achieved per recharge cycle. The robot must recharge when its battery level (40 units after the second explanation) is too low to guarantee a safe return trip to the charger after visiting another painting. Therefore, a recharge is performed after every two paintings are explained. Each `recharge` action is a necessary step to enable the subsequent set of goal actions.

5.  **Plan Execution**: The plan follows this "visit two, then recharge" cycle for the first 30 paintings. For the final painting, a single trip is made, as the overall goal is complete once it is explained. All `move` actions are necessary to position the robot to achieve the `explain_painting` goals, and all `recharge` actions are necessary to power those movements.

Here is a step-by-step explanation of the planning process, focusing on battery management and goal satisfaction.

The primary goal is to make the robot `tiago` explain all 31 paintings listed in the problem file. The main constraint is the robot's battery, which starts at 100 units. Each `move` action costs 20 units, and each `explain_painting` action costs 10 units. The robot can only recharge at the `home` location.

**1. Devising an Efficient Tour Strategy**

To minimize movements and recharges, the robot should explain multiple paintings per trip before returning to `home`. A single trip is called a "tour". We need to find the maximum number of paintings the robot can explain in one tour.

*   **Cost Calculation:** A tour to explain `N` paintings involves:
    1.  One `move` from `home` to the first painting (P1).
    2.  `N-1` moves between paintings (P1 to P2, P2 to P3, etc.).
    3.  `N` `explain_painting` actions.
    4.  One final `move` from the last painting (PN) back to `home` to recharge.
*   **Total Battery Cost:** `(1 + (N-1) + 1) moves * 20 battery/move` + `N explanations * 10 battery/explanation`
    *   This simplifies to: `(N+1) * 20 + N * 10` = `20N + 20 + 10N` = `30N + 20`.
*   **Finding Maximum `N`:** The total cost must be less than or equal to the battery capacity (100).
    *   `30N + 20 <= 100`
    *   `30N <= 80`
    *   `N <= 2.66...`
*   **Conclusion:** The maximum number of paintings the robot can visit and explain in a single, complete tour (including returning home) is **2**.

**2. The Recharge Cycle**

Based on the calculation, the optimal strategy is to perform tours of 2 paintings at a time.

*   **Tour Cost:** A 2-painting tour costs `30*2 + 20 = 80` battery units.
*   **Recharge Necessity:** After completing a 2-painting tour and returning to `home`, the robot will have `100 - 80 = 20` battery units remaining. While this is enough to perform another `move` action, it is not enough to complete another tour. Therefore, upon arriving at `home`, the robot must execute the `recharge` action to restore its battery to 100 before starting the next tour. This is a necessary recharge to continue its mission.

**3. Plan Structure**

The complete plan is structured as follows:

*   **Initial Action:** The plan starts with `(start_welcome tiago)`.
*   **Main Loops:** There are 31 paintings in total. The plan will execute 15 tours, each explaining 2 paintings. This covers `15 * 2 = 30` paintings. Each of these tours follows the pattern: `move -> explain -> move -> explain -> move_to_home -> recharge`.
*   **Final Action:** After 30 paintings are explained, the robot is at `home` with a full battery. For the final (31st) painting, it only needs to travel to the location and explain it. An unnecessary return trip to `home` is avoided to maximize efficiency, as the goal is met once the last painting is explained.

Each `explain_painting` action is included in the plan because the goal is to have all paintings explained (`(explained_painting ...)` for every location). The plan systematically visits each location to satisfy these goals.

INICIANDO GENERACIÓN CON: MOONSHOTAI/KIMI-K2-INSTRUCT-0905
Generando plan PDDL con moonshotai/kimi-k2-instruct-0905...
==================================================
Step-by-step reasoning while planning:

1. Battery budget: 100 units.  
   Move = –20, Explain = –10, Recharge = reset to 100 (5 s, must be on a charger).  
   We must never drop below 20 while moving or below 10 while explaining.

2. Goal: explain every painting location.  
   There are 30 painting locations (all except home).  
   We start at home (charger), battery 100.

3. Greedy grouping:  
   - Do as many explanations as possible between recharges.  
   - After every 4 explanations we have spent 4·10 = 40, plus the moves to reach them.  
   - The cheapest cycle is:  
     home → L1 → L2 → L3 → L4 → home (recharge).  
     Moves: 5·20 = 100, explanations: 4·10 = 40 → total 140, but we refill after 100 spent, so we need to refill after 4 explanations (battery 20 left when we arrive home).

4. Repeat the cycle for the next 4 paintings, etc.  
   30 paintings ⇒ 8 cycles of 4 paintings (24) + one cycle of 6 paintings (the last group we do 6 before returning).

5. Detailed battery check for the first group (positions 1-4):
   start 100  
   move home→1 (80)  
   explain 1 (70)  
   move 1→2 (50)  
   explain 2 (40)  
   move 2→3 (20)  ← still ≥20, safe  
   explain 3 (10)  
   move 3→4 (–10) → would become –10 ❌  
   Therefore we must recharge after the 3rd explanation in this group; we do it at position 3 (which is not a charger). Instead we change strategy: after 3 explanations we return to home (battery 20), recharge, then continue.  
   This generalises to: every 3 explanations we return to home and recharge.

6. Final pattern:
   - 3 explanations ⇒ return home ⇒ recharge (5 s)  
   - 30 explanations ⇒ 10 such triplets ⇒ 10 recharges.

Step-by-step reasoning while planning:

1. Start: battery = 100, at home (charger).
2. Goal is to explain every painting.  
   The paintings that appear in the problem are exactly the 30 locations that are not “home”.  
   Therefore the planner must visit and explain all 30 of them.

3. Battery budget per “useful” move:
   - 20 to move to a painting location.
   - 10 to explain it.
   - 20 to leave that location.
   ⇒ 50 battery are consumed for every painting that is actually explained.  
   With 100 battery we can therefore do two full paintings (2×50 = 100) before we are empty.

4. Recharge policy:
   - After the second explanation we have 0 battery left, so we must be at a charger before we attempt the next move.
   - The only charger in the problem is “home”.
   - Hence, after every second explanation we return to home, recharge once (5 s), and immediately start the next pair.

5. Sequence that follows:
   - Pair 1: move→explain→move→explain (battery 100→0).
   - Return to home, recharge (battery 0→100).
   - Pair 2: move→explain→move→explain (battery 100→0).
   - Return to home, recharge … and so on for 15 complete pairs (30 paintings).

6. No extra moves or recharges are ever required; the above pattern is optimal in number of actions and total time.

Step-by-step reasoning while planning:

1. Battery budget: start at 100.  
   - Each move costs 20 → after 5 moves battery = 0.  
   - Each explain costs 10 → after 10 explains battery = 0.  
   - Recharge is only possible at home (the only charger).  
   - Recharge takes 5 s and resets battery to 100.  
   - Objective: explain every painting location (all 30 locations must have explained_painting = true).

2. Since we must visit 30 locations and explain each, we need at least 30 explains (300 battery) plus the moves to reach them.  
   - 100 battery units allow 5 moves (100/20).  
   - Therefore, after every 5 moves we must return to home to recharge.  
   - While at a location we can explain it (cost 10) without affecting the “moves-until-recharge” counter.

3. Planning strategy:  
   - Group locations into clusters of ≤5 moves from home.  
   - After each cluster, return to home, recharge, and start the next cluster.  
   - While inside a cluster, explain every location right after arriving.

4. Clustering (Manhattan-like distance on an implicit grid; here we just count moves):  
   Cluster 1 (4 moves): home → maestro_aprendiz → elgrito → guernica → la_joven_de_la_perla  
   Cluster 2 (4 moves): home → monalisa → noche_estrellada → las_meninas → el_3_de_mayo  
   Cluster 3 (4 moves): home → el_jardin → las_tres_gracias → la_rendicion → el_nacimiento  
   Cluster 4 (4 moves): home → la_creacion → la_ultima_cena → la_libertad → el_hijo  
   Cluster 5 (4 moves): home → american_gothic → la_persistencia → la_ronda → impresion_sol  
   Cluster 6 (4 moves): home → banistas → saturno → whistlers → la_gran_ola  
   Cluster 7 (4 moves): home → el_beso → autorretrato → el_carnaval → nighthawks  
   Cluster 8 (2 moves): home → retrato_adele → campbells → composition_viii  

   Each cluster keeps moves ≤5, so we never run out of battery before returning home.

5. Execution inside one cluster:  
   - Move to first location (cost 20).  
   - Explain it (cost 10).  
   - Repeat for next locations.  
   - After last location, move back to home (cost 20), recharge (cost 0, resets to 100).

6. All 30 locations are explained, so the goal is satisfied.
